  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_421735ca-92d1-4688-860a-f96d1197ca09'
      });
    }

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't think that they will understand the concept of all the codes because they are extremely complicated. There also is death and assassination etc<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't think that they will understand the concept of all the codes because they are extremely complicated. There also is death and assassination etc. so I don't think its a good book to read to a 4 year old. I read this at age 9 and thought it was confusing a bit.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12814023-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541716988p2/12814023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/429224163?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/12814023-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780007487509" href="/book/show/16050538-take-your-last-breath">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer429224163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5189501270583676127">I found that the second book in the Ruby Redfort series wasn't as good as the first, but it slowly got better and better until the end, when it left me wanting more. I loved how in this book, the reader learned more about the characters and you could see their personalities a bit more than in the first. Like in Look Into my Eyes, I loved hearing about the codes that were featured and seeing how they worked. I must say I'm very frustrated though because I still can't figure out what Ruby and Clan</span>
  <span id="freeText5189501270583676127" style="display:none">I found that the second book in the Ruby Redfort series wasn't as good as the first, but it slowly got better and better until the end, when it left me wanting more. I loved how in this book, the reader learned more about the characters and you could see their personalities a bit more than in the first. Like in Look Into my Eyes, I loved hearing about the codes that were featured and seeing how they worked. I must say I'm very frustrated though because I still can't figure out what Ruby and Clancy's new codeword is. I liked how the book was always exciting and how everything came together piece by piece. Definitely another one of my favourites! I can't wait for the third book! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5189501270583676127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer590845376505522785">This book was really good, but in my opinion, not as good as the first. <br/>It was really nice to see more into Ruby's town and see into her past. It was also nice to see that she really cares about her parents loads, as we didn't really see that in the first book. <br/>It was great to see the Count back, he is a really excellent stereotypical villain!!<br/>I didn't think this book's plot was as good, personally I preferred the last book's mystery much better.   <span id="freeText590845376505522785" style="display:none">This book was really good, but in my opinion, not as good as the first. <br />It was really nice to see more into Ruby's town and see into her past. It was also nice to see that she really cares about her parents loads, as we didn't really see that in the first book. <br />It was great to see the Count back, he is a really excellent stereotypical villain!!<br />I didn't think this book's plot was as good, personally I preferred the last book's mystery much better. This one seemed a bit TOO fantasy-like for me, about pirates and lost treasure. <br /><br />It was gripping, though, especially when Ruby was **SPOILERS** trying to piece together the White Noise code. <br />So glad Hitch is still around, he's an excellent character. <br /><br />All in all, an excellent read, and a nice balance of fast-paced plot and nice character history and personality development. <br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_626971862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/626971862" />
    <a title="Cleo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12749947-cleo"><img alt="Cleo" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/626971862?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cleo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cleo" href="/user/show/12749947-cleo">Cleo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12749947-cleo?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12749947-cleo?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12749947-cleo?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12749947-cleo?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer626971862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17117827357209053221">This is the sequel to Ruby Redfort, in which there is more mystery and a lot of deep-sea intrigue. "Everyone’s favorite girl detective is back for a second mind-blowing installment, packed with all the off-the-wall humor, action, and friendship of the first book. This time, though, it’s an adventure on the wide-open ocean, and Ruby is all at sea. . . . Can she crack the case of the Twinford pirates while evading the clutches of a vile sea monster as well as the evil Count von Viscount? Well, you</span>
  <span id="freeText17117827357209053221" style="display:none">This is the sequel to Ruby Redfort, in which there is more mystery and a lot of deep-sea intrigue. "Everyone’s favorite girl detective is back for a second mind-blowing installment, packed with all the off-the-wall humor, action, and friendship of the first book. This time, though, it’s an adventure on the wide-open ocean, and Ruby is all at sea. . . . Can she crack the case of the Twinford pirates while evading the clutches of a vile sea monster as well as the evil Count von Viscount? Well, you wouldn't want to bet against her." <br /><br />I certainly don't love this series, but it is entertaining and amusing, if very unrealistic. At least, I think it's unrealistic. There's nothing wrong with that though. It's a very fun series, although I haven't read the original picture books in which Ruby Redfort is first mentioned. To tell you the truth, I didn't remember much about the first book, even though I didn't read it that long ago. But still, it wasn't really necessary. Most of the main points of the previous book were re-summarized, and I quickly remembered the basics (if not the details) of Look Into My Eyes. Spoilers for it are somewhat inevitable. <br /><br />So, the book begins with Ruby, Spectrum's youngest agent, at a training camp by the ocean. She's learning to scuba dive. Ruby isn't afraid of sharks and other sea creatures...at least not yet. She's all in all enjoying the camp, except for a certain obnoxious officer. Anyway, it didn't seem realistic to me that a super top secret agency would be training its agents to...scuba dive. I mean, it certainly is a useful skill, but it's hardly spy-like. Most hard-boiled detective stories don't occur underwater. That was a bit confusing, but it set the stage for the rest of the book's mystery, which involves lost treasure (of course), pirates, and deep sea creatures. All a bit over-the-top, you might say, but certainly entertaining.<br /><br />Both the characters of Hitch and Clancy, Ruby's two main friends in the know, are very amusing to read about. I particularly like Hitch. Clancy is a bit strange, and the way he and Ruby talk to one another seems very unrealistic for two thirteen year olds. I mean, not many people talk like that anymore. Ruby's smart, but why must she insist on talking ungrammatically? However, if you just let yourself forget that aspect, Take Your Last Breath is certainly an enjoyable read. <br /><br />Another great thing about this series is that in both books, there are these little recurring things, and the reader isn't sure whether they're related to the mystery or not. For example, in Take Your Last Breath, the asteroid, the radio station being disrupted, the strange man hanging around town, and most particularly, the loose clasp on Ruby's escape watch. I wasn't sure whether that was incidental or would play a big part in the story later. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Spoiler: It did).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This kept me reading, and once you get into Take Your Last Breath, it's quite suspenseful and quite absorbing. The reader also gets to know Ruby's parents much better, and become more sympathetic to them. I would definitely recommend it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17117827357209053221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3219237435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3219237435" />
    <a title="Erin Pradeep" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/107446518-erin-pradeep"><img alt="Erin Pradeep" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606070666p2/107446518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3219237435?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin Pradeep" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin Pradeep" href="/user/show/107446518-erin-pradeep">Erin Pradeep</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3219237435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3650377787193793870">Take your Last Breath was for me a slight disappointment. When I read the initial book, I devoured it with a day, enthralled by the deep, sinister plot of the Count, and desperate for the second installment. Consequently, I hurriedly ordered it in the library and after a few days, it was in my hands. The beginning for me started out fine. I’ve heard that others found the opening quite slow, but the small quips and sarcastic remarks kept me going. Eventually, the small clues of crime began to app</span>
  <span id="freeText3650377787193793870" style="display:none">Take your Last Breath was for me a slight disappointment. When I read the initial book, I devoured it with a day, enthralled by the deep, sinister plot of the Count, and desperate for the second installment. Consequently, I hurriedly ordered it in the library and after a few days, it was in my hands. The beginning for me started out fine. I’ve heard that others found the opening quite slow, but the small quips and sarcastic remarks kept me going. Eventually, the small clues of crime began to appear, and Ruby’s next mission commenced, on finding the cause of the mayday disruption, the confusing tangle of trade ship destinations and the discovering of drowned people and carcasses of sea creatures. Is all this activity linked to one another or is there a minor connection which leads to a great crime?<br />After reading the book, a minor amount of my enjoyment for the book deteriorated, for two reasons:<br />1)	For me, some of the dialogue felt forced, in a silly way. For example,<br /><br /><i>‘Hitch was sitting at the kitchen table, polishing some silverware and looking for all the world like an actual butler.<br />“I think you may be getting too into your cover story,” said Ruby, her nose in the refrigerator, searching for the juice. <br />Hitch shrugged, “Miss Digby runs a tight ship”. <br />“Yeah, she already believes you’re a butler; you don’t need to make out you’re the best entire one to ever polish on this earthly universe of Twinford.”<br />“And I don’t want her thinking I’m a lousy one either. My life wouldn’t be worth living kid.”<br />Ruby shrugged and sucked on her drinking straw.’</i><br /><br />I got slightly irritated by that. I don’t know whether it is meant to make me laugh. I mean, come one, Ruby! Who cares what he’s doing? Did you really have to make a conversation out of that?<br />Another scene was when Ruby pointed out that Clancy, her best friend, used the word ‘sweethearts’ in an ‘old lady-type’ of way. I really don’t care, just let him say that. He’s still awesome! Just because he used ‘sweethearts’ in a different ‘uncool’ context, doesn’t mean you need to point it out!<br /><br />2)	Another reason was the plot. It felt to fantasy-like, with the odd pirates, treasure, legends and rumours and even <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the giant octopus which is killing the people<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[. It just felt out of line.<br />Despite all this bad, I still enjoyed it. Clancy and his extreme fear of the ocean was the likely to be the most hilarious in the book. Miss Digby and Hitch are still the same, with their witty remarks and the Count remains evil. <br />Recommended.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="3650377787193793870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3123895787577807270" style="display:none">The Ruby Redfort series has now become one of my favourites. In this second instalment, 'Take Your Last Breath', I was once again brought into the world of Ruby Redfort, Clancy Crew and Spectrum. Each book comes with a new and exciting plot line that engages the reader in an interactive way.<br /><br />'Take Your Last Breath' was full of mystery and humour the way all of Lauren Child's works are and was a great escape into a world of a teenage spy. The plot may have been a bit predictable but it was a great mystery nonetheless. I also like the addition of notes on the static code of Chime Radio and Count von Viscount.<br /><br />Once again, I'd like to say that this book was quite enjoyable and I look forward to the next in the Ruby Redfort series. </span>

<div id="review_3362354824" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3362354824" />
    <a title="Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7106883-taylor"><img alt="Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358807685p2/7106883.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3362354824?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor" href="/user/show/7106883-taylor">Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7106883-taylor?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7106883-taylor?shelf=kid-lit">kid-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3362354824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12696020237018109047">Ruby Redfort is a code-breaking genius and at only 13 years of age has been recruited by the spy agency Spectrum because of her unique talents. In this book, odd occurrences have been piling up in her home town of Twinford and, with the help of her mentor Hitch and her best friend Clancy, Ruby sets out to get to the bottom of things. This was a fun book. As a middle-aged woman, I am sure I am not the target audience for this series of books but I did really enjoy it and think my adolescent self </span>
  <span id="freeText12696020237018109047" style="display:none">Ruby Redfort is a code-breaking genius and at only 13 years of age has been recruited by the spy agency Spectrum because of her unique talents. In this book, odd occurrences have been piling up in her home town of Twinford and, with the help of her mentor Hitch and her best friend Clancy, Ruby sets out to get to the bottom of things. This was a fun book. As a middle-aged woman, I am sure I am not the target audience for this series of books but I did really enjoy it and think my adolescent self would have enjoyed it as well. Ruby is sort of a cross between Nancy Drew and Flavia de Luce although leaning more towards the Flavia end of the spectrum. She is brilliant and saucy and the book has a number of interesting supporting characters. My favourites were Ruby's well-intended but dim-witted parents who have only vague notions of what parenting entails. Thank you to Goodreads Giveaways for the chance to read this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12696020237018109047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483978369?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriella" href="/user/show/71957915-gabriella">Gabriella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71957915-gabriella?shelf=year-5">year-5</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483978369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18146020060938641312">I enjoyed this book, however, I thought the pace of it was quite slow and a lot of the plot was quite repetitive. I thought the outcome of the plot was quite disappointing for the length of the book and the build-up to the solution of the many mysteries discussed. I thought I would be gripped from start to finish with this book as the blurb sounded very interesting, however, I was often left waiting for twists and turns in the book that never was delivered. I think children would want to read th</span>
  <span id="freeText18146020060938641312" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book, however, I thought the pace of it was quite slow and a lot of the plot was quite repetitive. I thought the outcome of the plot was quite disappointing for the length of the book and the build-up to the solution of the many mysteries discussed. I thought I would be gripped from start to finish with this book as the blurb sounded very interesting, however, I was often left waiting for twists and turns in the book that never was delivered. I think children would want to read this book as it is about a spy and her adventures. I think this book is good as it flips gender stereotypes on its head as the girl is a spy and the heroine, not the boy. Although I didn't enjoy the book as much as I thought I would I still would recommend this to children as I think the plot is a little different to what I have normally come across with children's books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18146020060938641312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

The challenge she had to take is that she had to swim underwater. But when she did, something went wrong and she had to breathe without oxygen. </span>
  <span id="freeText18152328181597895737" style="display:none">Something weird is going on at the sea. There was a rumour that a fisherman was drowned and strangled. A lot of strange sea sounds like someone calling for help from underwater. There were unusual marine activities like dead whales, sharks in bay, seagulls flocking inland, etc. Ruby is determined to find out what was going on and put things right again. The challenge she had to take is that she had to swim underwater. But when she did, something went wrong and she had to breathe without oxygen. What I don't like about this book is that there is only a little bit of conversation. What I like about this book though, is that there are a lot of challenges. I'd give it a 9.5/10</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_25394458'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25394458-the-whispers-in-the-walls"><img alt="The Whispers in the Walls (Scarlet and Ivy, #2)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1429876783l/25394458._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+UeGXMORBzRqbx8TtEUUxyRB2TkrVjUxIZhBljn4ZUhbOw3Zzs0OzJcrBjaVXsLU1PjQ6m/zlSttNHK6ceSuRw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/42016.Lauren_Child">About Lauren Child</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/42016.Lauren_Child"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_111x148-8060b12280b2aec7543bafb574ee8422.png);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/42016.Lauren_Child">Lauren Child

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1914877380089687004"><b>Lauren Child</b> MBE is an English author and illustrator. She was the UK Children's Laureate from 2017-19.<br/><br/>Child grew up in Wiltshire as the middle child of three sisters and the daughter of two teachers. She has always been interested in the many aspects of childhood, from gazing into toy shop windows to watching American children's shows from the 1960s. After attending two Art Schools, she travelled</span>
  <span id="freeText1914877380089687004" style="display:none"><b>Lauren Child</b> MBE is an English author and illustrator. She was the UK Children's Laureate from 2017-19.<br /><br />Child grew up in Wiltshire as the middle child of three sisters and the daughter of two teachers. She has always been interested in the many aspects of childhood, from gazing into toy shop windows to watching American children's shows from the 1960s. After attending two Art Schools, she travelled for six months, still unsure about which career to embark upon. <br /><br />Before writing and illustrating children's books Child started her own company 'Chandeliers for the People' making lampshades. It was only when she came to write and illustrate the book <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/267634.Clarice_Bean__That_s_Me" title="Clarice Bean, That's Me" rel="nofollow noopener">Clarice Bean, That's Me</a>
</i> that she decided to devote her time to writing and illustrating books for children, which combines her fascination for childhood and her talent for designing and creating. Child gets her inspiration from other people's conversations or from seeing something funny happen. <br /><br />Her book <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/137045.I_Will_Not_Ever_Never_Eat_A_Tomato" title="I Will Not Ever Never Eat A Tomato" rel="nofollow noopener">I Will Not Ever Never Eat A Tomato</a>
</i> won the 2000 Kate Greenaway Medal. For the 50th anniversary of the Medal (1955–2005), a panel named it one of the top ten winning works, which comprised the shortlist for a public vote for the nation's favourite. It finished third in the public vote from that shortlist.<br /><br />Child lives in North London. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1914877380089687004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
